# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 5: Equity & Inclusion in Economic Development:




### Introduction

In the previous chapters, we have explored the concepts of equity and inclusion, and their importance in creating a just city. We have also discussed the role of local policies in promoting equity and inclusion, and how they can be used as tools for economic development. In this chapter, we will delve deeper into the topic of equity and inclusion plans, which are crucial for the successful implementation of these policies.

Equity and inclusion plans are strategic documents that outline the steps and actions that a city will take to promote equity and inclusion among its residents. These plans are developed through a collaborative process that involves community members, government officials, and other stakeholders. They are essential for creating a just city, as they provide a roadmap for addressing the systemic barriers and disparities that exist in society.

In this chapter, we will discuss the importance of equity and inclusion plans, their development process, and the key components that should be included in these plans. We will also explore case studies of successful equity and inclusion plans from different cities, highlighting the strategies and approaches that have been effective in promoting equity and inclusion. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the role of equity and inclusion plans in creating a just city and how they can be used to promote economic development.




### Section: 5.1 Equity & Inclusion Plans:

Equity and inclusion plans are crucial for promoting equity and inclusion in a just city. These plans outline the steps and actions that a city will take to address systemic barriers and disparities among its residents. In this section, we will discuss the importance of equity and inclusion plans, their development process, and the key components that should be included in these plans.

#### 5.1a Understanding Equity and Inclusion

Equity and inclusion are closely related concepts that are essential for creating a just city. Equity refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities among all members of a community. It recognizes that certain groups, such as marginalized communities, have historically been disadvantaged and seeks to address these disparities. Inclusion, on the other hand, focuses on creating a welcoming and supportive environment for all members of a community. It recognizes that everyone has unique needs and seeks to accommodate these needs to ensure equal participation.

In the context of education, equity and inclusion have been widely discussed and implemented. The United Nations' Target 4 Goals, for example, emphasize the importance of education for all children, regardless of their social or economic background. In the United States, the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act (IDEA) and the No Child Left Behind Act (NCLB) have been enacted to ensure equal access to education for all students, including those with disabilities and those from disadvantaged backgrounds.

However, despite these efforts, there are still significant disparities in education outcomes for marginalized communities. For example, students from low-income families and students of color are more likely to attend under-resourced schools and have less access to quality education. This highlights the need for equity and inclusion plans to address these systemic barriers and promote equal opportunities for all students.

#### 5.1b The Development Process of Equity and Inclusion Plans

The development of equity and inclusion plans is a collaborative process that involves community members, government officials, and other stakeholders. It is important for all stakeholders to be involved in the process to ensure that the plan reflects the needs and concerns of the community. The process typically involves the following steps:

1. Identifying the target population: The first step in developing an equity and inclusion plan is to identify the target population. This could include marginalized communities, low-income families, or students with disabilities.

2. Conducting a needs assessment: A needs assessment is a crucial step in understanding the specific needs and concerns of the target population. This could involve surveys, focus groups, and data analysis.

3. Setting goals and objectives: Based on the needs assessment, goals and objectives for the equity and inclusion plan can be set. These should be specific, measurable, achievable, relevant, and time-bound (SMART).

4. Developing strategies and actions: The next step is to develop strategies and actions that will help achieve the goals and objectives. These could include policy changes, resource allocation, and community engagement.

5. Implementing and monitoring the plan: Once the plan is developed, it needs to be implemented and monitored to ensure its effectiveness. This could involve regular progress reports, evaluations, and adjustments to the plan as needed.

#### 5.1c Key Components of Equity and Inclusion Plans

Equity and inclusion plans should include the following key components to be effective:

1. A clear definition of equity and inclusion: It is important for the plan to clearly define what equity and inclusion mean in the context of the community. This will help guide the development of goals and strategies.

2. A focus on systemic barriers: Equity and inclusion plans should address systemic barriers that contribute to disparities among different groups. This could include policies, practices, and structures that need to be changed.

3. A commitment to data-driven decision making: Data and evidence are crucial for understanding the needs and concerns of the target population. Equity and inclusion plans should incorporate data analysis and use this information to inform decision making.

4. A focus on community engagement: Equity and inclusion plans should involve community members in the development and implementation process. This will help ensure that the plan reflects the needs and concerns of the community.

5. A commitment to continuous improvement: Equity and inclusion plans should be seen as a living document that is constantly evolving and improving. This will allow for adjustments and updates as needed to address emerging issues and concerns.

In conclusion, equity and inclusion plans are essential for promoting equity and inclusion in a just city. They require a collaborative and data-driven approach to address systemic barriers and disparities among different groups. By including key components such as a clear definition of equity and inclusion, a focus on systemic barriers, and community engagement, these plans can be effective in promoting equal opportunities for all members of a community.





### Related Context
```
# Debt-to-equity ratio

## Example

General Electric Co # Personal equity plan

A personal equity plan (PEP) was a form of tax-privileged investment account in the United Kingdom, available between 1986 and 1999.

## History

The plans were introduced by Nigel Lawson in the 1986 budget to encourage equity ownership among the wider population. PEPs were allowed to contain collective investments such as unit trusts. The "single company PEP", which was allowed to contain shares of a single company, was introduced in 1992. PEPs were superseded by individual savings accounts in 1999, and remaining accounts were converted to individual savings accounts in 2008.

## Types and privileges

Growth in a PEP was free from capital gains tax within the fund and on encashment. Income was free from income tax. When introduced in 1986, the fund was limited to £2,400 (annual allowance), but later increased to two types of PEP: the "general PEP" with an annual allowance of £6,000 and the "single company PEP" with an annual allowance of £3,000.

Investments in a general PEP were limited to qualifying collective investments. Qualifying investments had at least half of their assets invested in the UK, later extended to the European Union. The qualification rule for existing PEPs was removed in 2001. 

Single company PEPs could be invested in one company only. One way they could be used was to hold windfall shares received by members from mutual bodies when they became listed companies.

## Evolution

Beginning 6 April 1999, the Advanced Corporation Tax relief on share dividends received on a PEP was halved, partially ending their tax-exempt status. From 6 April 2004 all relief on dividends was removed, although no additional tax at the higher rate was due where otherwise it might have been. Gains on capital, and all other forms of income such as cash interest and bond income, remained tax-free. Significant cash holdings for any length of time were discouraged by HM Revenue and Customs; they would be subject to a 20% tax charge.

The PEP was replaced by the Individual Savings Account (ISA) in 1999. The ISA allows for a wider range of investments, including stocks and shares, cash, and even some types of life insurance. The annual allowance for an ISA is currently £20,000, and there is no longer a distinction between general and single company ISAs.

The PEP was a significant step in promoting equity and inclusion in the UK. It allowed individuals to invest in the stock market with tax advantages, encouraging them to become more financially literate and take control of their own financial future. However, the PEP was not without its flaws, and its replacement by the ISA has allowed for a more flexible and inclusive approach to investing.


### Last textbook section content:

#### 5.1a Understanding Equity and Inclusion

Equity and inclusion are crucial concepts in creating a just city. Equity refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities among all members of a community. It recognizes that certain groups, such as marginalized communities, have historically been disadvantaged and seeks to address these disparities. Inclusion, on the other hand, focuses on creating a welcoming and supportive environment for all members of a community. It recognizes that everyone has unique needs and seeks to accommodate these needs to ensure equal participation.

In the context of education, equity and inclusion have been widely discussed and implemented. The United Nations' Target 4 Goals, for example, emphasize the importance of education for all children, regardless of their social or economic background. In the United States, the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act (IDEA) and the No Child Left Behind Act (NCLB) have been enacted to ensure equal access to education for all students, including those with disabilities and those from disadvantaged backgrounds.

However, despite these efforts, there are still significant disparities in education outcomes for marginalized communities. For example, students from low-income families and students of color are more likely to attend under-resourced schools and have less access to quality education. This highlights the need for equity and inclusion plans to address these systemic barriers and promote equal opportunities for all students.

#### 5.1b Developing and Implementing Equity Plans

Equity plans are essential tools for promoting equity and inclusion in a just city. These plans outline the steps and actions that a city will take to address systemic barriers and disparities among its residents. They are developed through a collaborative process that involves community members, government officials, and other stakeholders.

The first step in developing an equity plan is to identify the target population. This could include marginalized communities, such as low-income families, students of color, or individuals with disabilities. Once the target population is identified, the next step is to conduct a needs assessment to understand the specific barriers and disparities faced by this group.

The needs assessment should involve community members from the target population to ensure that their voices are heard and their needs are addressed. It should also consider data and research to provide a comprehensive understanding of the issues at hand.

Once the needs assessment is complete, the next step is to develop strategies and actions to address the identified barriers and disparities. This could include policies, programs, and initiatives that promote equity and inclusion. For example, a city could implement a policy to provide free or reduced-cost education for low-income students, or create a program to support students with disabilities in their academic and social development.

The final step in developing an equity plan is to implement and monitor its progress. This involves allocating resources and assigning responsibilities to ensure that the plan is carried out effectively. It also involves regularly evaluating the plan's impact and making adjustments as needed.

In conclusion, equity and inclusion plans are crucial for promoting equity and inclusion in a just city. They are developed through a collaborative process and involve identifying the target population, conducting a needs assessment, developing strategies and actions, and implementing and monitoring progress. By addressing systemic barriers and disparities, these plans can create a more equitable and inclusive society for all residents.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the importance of equity and inclusion plans in promoting economic development and creating a just city. We have discussed the various components of these plans, including identifying target populations, setting goals and objectives, and implementing strategies to address systemic barriers. We have also examined the role of local policies in supporting and enforcing these plans.

Equity and inclusion plans are crucial for creating a more equitable and inclusive society, where all members have equal access to opportunities and resources. By addressing the needs and concerns of marginalized communities, these plans can help reduce disparities and promote economic growth. Additionally, by involving community members in the planning process, these plans can foster a sense of ownership and empowerment, leading to more sustainable and effective solutions.

As we have seen, equity and inclusion plans are not a one-size-fits-all solution. Each city and community has its own unique challenges and needs, and therefore, these plans must be tailored to address the specific issues at hand. By continuously evaluating and adjusting these plans, we can ensure that they remain relevant and effective in promoting equity and inclusion.

## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

### Introduction:

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become increasingly important in shaping the policies and strategies of local governments. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is crucial for policymakers to address the issues of equity and inclusion in order to create a just and sustainable city for all its residents. This chapter will explore the various aspects of equity and inclusion, and how they can be effectively integrated into local policies and strategies for economic development.

Equity and inclusion are closely intertwined concepts that aim to promote fairness and equality in society. Equity refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities among all members of a community, while inclusion focuses on creating a welcoming and supportive environment for all individuals, regardless of their background or characteristics. In the context of local policies and strategies, equity and inclusion play a crucial role in promoting economic development and creating a just city.

This chapter will delve into the different dimensions of equity and inclusion, including race, ethnicity, gender, and socioeconomic status. It will also examine the various factors that contribute to inequality and exclusion, such as systemic discrimination and unequal access to resources. By understanding these dimensions and factors, policymakers can develop more effective and targeted policies and strategies to address equity and inclusion issues.

Furthermore, this chapter will explore the relationship between equity and inclusion and economic development. It will discuss how promoting equity and inclusion can lead to increased economic growth and prosperity, as well as how economic development can be used as a tool to address issues of equity and inclusion. By understanding this relationship, policymakers can develop more comprehensive and sustainable policies and strategies for economic development.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive guide for policymakers on how to effectively integrate equity and inclusion into local policies and strategies for economic development. By understanding the various aspects of equity and inclusion, as well as their relationship with economic development, policymakers can create a more just and sustainable city for all its residents. 


## Chapter 6: Equity and Inclusion:




### Section: 5.1 Equity & Inclusion Plans:

#### 5.1c Evaluating the Impact of Equity Plans

After the development and implementation of equity plans, it is crucial to evaluate their impact. This evaluation process involves assessing the effectiveness of the plans in achieving their intended goals and identifying areas for improvement. 

#### 5.1c.1 Methods of Evaluation

There are several methods that can be used to evaluate the impact of equity plans. These include:

- **Surveys and Interviews**: Surveys and interviews can be used to gather feedback from stakeholders, including community members, businesses, and government agencies. This feedback can provide valuable insights into the perceived effectiveness of the plans and identify areas for improvement.

- **Data Analysis**: Data analysis can be used to assess the impact of equity plans on various indicators, such as income inequality, employment rates, and housing affordability. This can involve comparing data before and after the implementation of the plans, as well as comparing data in areas with and without the plans.

- **Case Studies**: Case studies can be used to examine the impact of equity plans in specific contexts. This can involve studying the implementation of the plans in different communities or industries, and assessing their effectiveness in these contexts.

#### 5.1c.2 Key Considerations in Evaluation

When evaluating the impact of equity plans, it is important to consider several key factors. These include:

- **Timing**: The timing of the evaluation is crucial. It should be conducted after the plans have been in place for a sufficient period of time to allow for their impact to be observed. However, it should also be conducted before significant changes occur that could affect the results of the evaluation.

- **Scope**: The scope of the evaluation should be broad enough to capture the full impact of the plans, but not so broad that it becomes unwieldy. This may involve focusing on specific aspects of the plans, such as their impact on a particular community or industry.

- **Stakeholder Involvement**: Stakeholder involvement is crucial in the evaluation process. This can involve involving stakeholders in the design of the evaluation, as well as in the interpretation and implementation of the results.

#### 5.1c.3 Challenges and Limitations

Despite the importance of evaluating the impact of equity plans, there are several challenges and limitations that can affect the process. These include:

- **Data Limitations**: As noted in the related context, there can be limitations in the data available for evaluation. This can include data that is incomplete, outdated, or difficult to access.

- **Complexity of Equity Plans**: Equity plans can be complex and multifaceted, making it difficult to isolate the impact of individual components. This can make it challenging to assess the effectiveness of the plans.

- **Political and Social Factors**: The impact of equity plans can be influenced by a variety of political and social factors, which can be difficult to control for in the evaluation process. This can include changes in government policies, economic conditions, and community dynamics.

Despite these challenges, evaluating the impact of equity plans is crucial for ensuring that they are achieving their intended goals and for making necessary improvements. It is also important for building support for equity plans and for promoting a culture of continuous improvement in equity and inclusion efforts.




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the importance of equity and inclusion plans in promoting economic development and creating a just city. We have discussed the various components of these plans, including needs assessments, community engagement, and policy recommendations. We have also examined the role of local governments in implementing these plans and the potential challenges and barriers they may face.

Equity and inclusion plans are crucial for addressing systemic inequalities and promoting fairness in our communities. By involving diverse stakeholders in the planning process, we can ensure that the needs and perspectives of all community members are considered. Additionally, by implementing evidence-based policies and programs, we can create more equitable and inclusive cities for all.

As we have seen, local policy-driven strategies play a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in our communities. By utilizing these strategies, we can create more just and prosperous cities for all residents. However, it is important to note that these plans must be continuously evaluated and updated to address changing needs and challenges.

In conclusion, equity and inclusion plans are essential for promoting economic development and creating a just city. By involving diverse stakeholders, utilizing evidence-based policies and programs, and continuously evaluating and updating these plans, we can create more equitable and inclusive communities for all.

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 6: Equity & Inclusion in Education:




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the complex and often contentious topic of race and gender-based approaches to equity. As we have seen in previous chapters, equity and inclusion are crucial components of a just city and economic development. However, the intersection of race and gender adds a layer of complexity to these discussions, as these factors have historically been used to marginalize and exclude certain groups from full participation in society.

We will explore the historical context of race and gender-based discrimination and how it has shaped our current understanding of equity. We will also examine the role of policy in addressing these issues, and how local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion for all members of the community.

This chapter will also discuss the importance of intersectionality in understanding and addressing race and gender-based approaches to equity. Intersectionality recognizes that individuals may face multiple forms of discrimination based on their intersecting identities, and that addressing one form of discrimination may not fully address all forms.

Finally, we will explore case studies and examples of successful race and gender-based equity initiatives, highlighting the importance of local policy and community involvement in promoting equity and inclusion. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a deeper understanding of the complexities of race and gender-based approaches to equity and the role of local policy in promoting a just city and economic development.




### Subsection: 6.1a Intersectionality and Equity

Intersectionality is a concept that has gained significant attention in recent years, particularly in the fields of race and gender studies. It is a framework that recognizes the complex and interconnected nature of social identities and the ways in which they intersect to create unique experiences of discrimination and marginalization. In this subsection, we will explore the concept of intersectionality and its relevance to equity and inclusion.

#### The Concept of Intersectionality

Intersectionality is a term coined by legal scholar Kimberlé Crenshaw in the 1980s to describe the ways in which different forms of discrimination intersect and compound each other. It recognizes that individuals may face multiple forms of discrimination based on their intersecting identities, such as race, gender, and social class. This concept challenges the idea that discrimination can be addressed by focusing on one form of identity at a time, and instead emphasizes the need to address the interconnectedness of these identities.

#### Intersectionality and Equity

Intersectionality plays a crucial role in understanding and addressing equity issues. As mentioned in the previous chapter, equity is about ensuring fairness and equal opportunities for all members of a community. However, the concept of equity is often limited to addressing one form of discrimination at a time, such as race or gender. This approach fails to recognize the ways in which these forms of discrimination intersect and compound each other, leading to a more complex and pervasive issue of equity.

Intersectionality allows us to see the ways in which race and gender intersect to create unique experiences of discrimination and marginalization. For example, a black woman may face discrimination and marginalization based on her race and gender, which may be compounded by her social class. This intersectionality of identities can have a significant impact on her opportunities and experiences in society.

#### Intersectionality and Policy

Policy plays a crucial role in addressing equity issues, and intersectionality must be considered in policy-making. Policies that focus on one form of discrimination at a time may fail to address the interconnectedness of different forms of discrimination. This can lead to ineffective or even harmful policies that do not adequately address the needs and experiences of individuals who face multiple forms of discrimination.

In order to create policies that are inclusive and equitable, it is essential to consider the intersectionality of different forms of discrimination. This requires a deep understanding of the ways in which these identities intersect and compound each other, as well as a commitment to addressing these issues in a comprehensive and holistic manner.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, intersectionality is a crucial concept in understanding and addressing equity issues. It recognizes the complex and interconnected nature of social identities and the ways in which they intersect to create unique experiences of discrimination and marginalization. In order to create policies that are inclusive and equitable, it is essential to consider the intersectionality of different forms of discrimination and address them in a comprehensive and holistic manner. 





### Subsection: 6.1b Racial and Gender Disparities

Racial and gender disparities are a significant aspect of equity and inclusion, as they have a profound impact on the lives of individuals and communities. These disparities are often interconnected, with race and gender intersecting to create unique experiences of discrimination and marginalization. In this subsection, we will explore the concept of racial and gender disparities and their implications for equity and inclusion.

#### The Concept of Racial and Gender Disparities

Racial and gender disparities refer to the unequal treatment and outcomes experienced by individuals based on their race and gender. These disparities can manifest in various aspects of life, including education, employment, healthcare, and criminal justice. For instance, studies have shown that black and Hispanic students are more likely to be suspended or expelled from school than their white peers, and that women are underrepresented in leadership positions in many industries (Crenshaw, 1989).

#### The Intersection of Race and Gender

The intersection of race and gender can exacerbate these disparities. For example, black women are particularly underrepresented in the field of computing. A 2021 study found that only 5% of computer science majors in the United States are Asian women, 2% are Latina women, and 2% are Black women. This underrepresentation is even more pronounced in the technology industry, where black women are less likely to be promoted to executive positions compared to white women (Crenshaw, 1989).

#### Addressing Racial and Gender Disparities

Addressing racial and gender disparities requires a comprehensive approach that recognizes the interconnectedness of these disparities. This includes policies and initiatives that promote diversity and inclusion, as well as efforts to address systemic racism and sexism. For instance, community colleges have been found to play a key role in incorporating more women into STEM majors, due to their accessibility and opportunities for upward transfer into higher education and the workforce.

In conclusion, racial and gender disparities are a significant aspect of equity and inclusion, and addressing them requires a nuanced understanding of the interconnectedness of race and gender. By promoting diversity and inclusion, and addressing systemic racism and sexism, we can work towards creating a more equitable and inclusive society for all.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex and multifaceted nature of race and gender-based approaches to equity. We have delved into the historical, social, and economic factors that contribute to the disparities faced by marginalized communities, particularly those based on race and gender. We have also examined the role of policy in addressing these disparities, and the importance of local, community-driven strategies in promoting equity and inclusion.

We have seen how race and gender-based approaches to equity are not just about addressing individual experiences, but also about challenging systemic and institutionalized discrimination. We have also discussed the importance of intersectionality in understanding and addressing these issues, as race and gender are not isolated factors but intersect in complex ways to shape individuals' experiences.

Finally, we have highlighted the importance of local policy-driven strategies in promoting equity and inclusion. These strategies, when implemented effectively, can have a significant impact on the lives of marginalized communities, and contribute to the creation of more just and inclusive cities.

## Chapter: Chapter 7: Disability & Age Approaches to Equity

### Introduction

In this chapter, we delve into the critical aspects of disability and age approaches to equity. The chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of how these two factors intersect and influence the economic development and creation of just cities. 

Disability and age are two significant factors that can significantly impact an individual's life. They can influence one's ability to access education, employment, healthcare, and other essential services. Moreover, they can also shape one's social interactions and overall quality of life. 

The chapter will explore the various ways in which disability and age can be approached from an equity perspective. It will discuss the challenges faced by individuals with disabilities and the elderly in accessing opportunities and services, and the policies and strategies that can be implemented to address these challenges. 

Furthermore, the chapter will also delve into the role of local policies in promoting equity for individuals with disabilities and the elderly. It will examine how these policies can be designed and implemented to create more inclusive and accessible cities, where all individuals, regardless of their disability or age, can participate fully and equally. 

Finally, the chapter will discuss the importance of community engagement and participation in promoting equity for individuals with disabilities and the elderly. It will explore how community-driven strategies can be used to address the unique needs and challenges faced by these groups, and to create more equitable and inclusive cities.

In essence, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of disability and age approaches to equity, and to equip readers with the knowledge and tools to promote equity for individuals with disabilities and the elderly in their local communities.




### Subsection: 6.1c Strategies for Addressing Race and Gender Inequities

Addressing race and gender inequities requires a multifaceted approach that addresses the root causes of these disparities. In this subsection, we will explore some strategies that can be used to address these inequities.

#### Policy Interventions

Policy interventions can play a crucial role in addressing race and gender inequities. For instance, policies can be implemented to promote diversity and inclusion in various sectors, such as education, employment, and healthcare. These policies can include affirmative action programs, which aim to increase the representation of underrepresented groups in these sectors (Crenshaw, 1989).

#### Education and Awareness

Education and awareness are also key strategies for addressing race and gender inequities. By educating individuals about the history and impact of racism and sexism, we can increase their understanding of these issues and promote more inclusive behaviors. Awareness campaigns can also be used to raise awareness about these issues and promote a sense of responsibility among individuals to address these inequities (Crenshaw, 1989).

#### Intersectional Approaches

Given the interconnectedness of race and gender, intersectional approaches are often necessary to address race and gender inequities. These approaches recognize that individuals can experience multiple forms of discrimination based on their intersecting identities, and aim to address these inequities in a holistic manner (Crenshaw, 1989).

#### Addressing Systemic Inequities

Finally, addressing systemic inequities is crucial for addressing race and gender inequities. This can involve addressing structural barriers that limit the opportunities available to certain groups, as well as promoting policies and practices that promote equity and inclusion (Crenshaw, 1989).

In conclusion, addressing race and gender inequities requires a comprehensive approach that addresses the root causes of these disparities. By implementing policy interventions, promoting education and awareness, using intersectional approaches, and addressing systemic inequities, we can work towards creating a more equitable and inclusive society for all individuals.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have delved into the complex and multifaceted issues of race and gender in the context of equity and inclusion. We have explored how these factors can influence economic development and the creation of just cities. We have also examined various strategies and policies that can be implemented to address these issues and promote equity and inclusion.

We have seen that race and gender are not just social constructs, but they have a profound impact on the lives of individuals and communities. They can shape opportunities, limit possibilities, and create barriers to economic development and the creation of just cities. However, we have also learned that these issues can be addressed through policy-driven strategies that promote equity and inclusion.

We have discussed the importance of diversity and inclusion in economic development and the creation of just cities. We have also highlighted the need for policies that promote equal opportunities and treatment for all individuals, regardless of their race or gender. We have also emphasized the importance of creating an environment where everyone feels valued, respected, and included.

In conclusion, race and gender are critical factors in the pursuit of equity and inclusion. They require careful consideration and a comprehensive approach that involves policy-driven strategies, diversity and inclusion initiatives, and a commitment to creating a just city for all.

#### Exercise 1

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 7: Equity & Inclusion in Economic Development:




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the intersection of environmental justice and equity planning in the context of local policy-driven strategies for economic development and the just city. Environmental justice is a concept that has gained significant attention in recent years, as it addresses the unequal distribution of environmental benefits and burdens among different communities. Equity planning, on the other hand, is a process that aims to ensure fair and just distribution of resources and opportunities among all members of a community.

The combination of these two concepts is crucial in creating a just and sustainable city. As we have seen in previous chapters, economic development is a key factor in creating a thriving city. However, it is important to consider the impact of economic development on the environment and the different communities within the city. This is where environmental justice and equity planning come into play.

In this chapter, we will delve into the various aspects of environmental justice and equity planning, including the history and evolution of these concepts, their importance in creating a just city, and the challenges and opportunities they present. We will also explore the role of local policies and strategies in addressing environmental justice and equity issues, and how they can be used to promote sustainable and equitable economic development.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of environmental justice and equity planning, and their crucial role in creating a just and sustainable city. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complexities of these concepts and their importance in creating a thriving and equitable city. 


# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter: - Chapter 7: Environmental Justice & Equity Planning:




### Related Context
```
# Environmental planning

## Environmental Justice

Environmental justice is the equitable inclusion and treatment of all human beings in all aspects of environmental planning, as well as in the enforcement of environmental legislation. It is increasingly recognized as a key part of environmental planning. Environmental justice issues are usually fought within communities to establish environmentally-friendly and accessible neighborhoods and living conditions, and to improve the local ecology. The Environmental Protection Agency has declared it essential that residents should play an active role in the reshaping of their neighborhoods.  Many levels of government and international organizations agree on the need for equitable and sustainable housing and transportation, as core characteristics of environmental justice; these are considered today a part of the battle against the climate crisis. Environmental activists act as watchdogs on government support for the battles of underrepresented communities against environmental hazards that threaten their health or way of life.

### United States

In the United States of America, there have been numerous examples of the state provisioning of environmental justice in multiple communities. Listed are some of such projects:

 # Environmental justice

### Europe

The European Environment Agency (EEA) reports that exposure to environmental harms such as pollution is correlated with poverty, and that poorer countries suffer from environmental harms while higher income countries produce the majority of the pollution. Western Europe has more extensive evidence of environmental inequality.

Romani peoples are ethnic minorities that experience environmental discrimination. Discriminatory laws force Romani people In many countries to live in slums or ghettos with poor access to running water and sewage, or where they are exposed to hazardous wastes.

The European Union is trying to strive towards environmental justice by putting into action the Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union, which includes the right to a high level of environmental protection and the right to access to information on the environment. The EU also has the Environmental Liability Directive, which aims to ensure that those responsible for environmental damage are held accountable. Additionally, the EU has the Environmental Impact Assessment Directive, which requires environmental assessments for certain projects that may have significant environmental impacts.

### Conclusion

Environmental justice is a crucial aspect of environmental planning and is essential for creating a just and sustainable city. It is important for local policies and strategies to address environmental justice issues and promote equitable and sustainable development. The United States and the European Union have made efforts towards environmental justice, but there is still much work to be done. As we continue to face environmental challenges, it is crucial that we prioritize environmental justice and ensure that all communities have equal access to a clean and healthy environment.


# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter: - Chapter 7: Environmental Justice & Equity Planning:




### Section: 7.1 Environmental Justice & Equity Planning:

Environmental justice and equity planning are crucial components of creating a just and sustainable city. As discussed in the previous section, environmental racism and disparities in access to clean air and water have been well-documented in the United States. These injustices have significant impacts on the health and well-being of communities, particularly those that are already marginalized and disadvantaged.

#### 7.1a The Role of Environmental Justice and Equity Planning in Local Policy

Local policy plays a critical role in addressing environmental justice and equity issues. It is at the local level that policies can be tailored to the specific needs and characteristics of a community. This allows for a more targeted and effective approach to addressing environmental inequalities and disparities.

One of the key ways in which local policy can address environmental justice and equity is through the implementation of environmental impact assessments (EIAs). EIAs are a tool used to evaluate the potential environmental impacts of a proposed project or policy. They can help identify potential environmental hazards and inform decision-making processes to mitigate these impacts. By incorporating EIAs into local policy, communities can ensure that new developments and policies do not exacerbate existing environmental inequalities.

Another important aspect of local policy is the consideration of environmental justice in decision-making processes. This can be achieved through the inclusion of environmental justice impact assessments (EJIAs) in policy development. EJIAs are a more comprehensive version of EIAs that specifically focus on the potential environmental justice impacts of a proposed project or policy. By conducting EJIAs, communities can ensure that the potential impacts on marginalized and disadvantaged communities are carefully considered and addressed.

In addition to these tools, local policy can also incorporate principles of environmental justice and equity into its overall framework. This can include policies that prioritize the protection and improvement of environmental quality in disadvantaged communities, as well as policies that promote equitable access to environmental benefits such as parks and green spaces. By incorporating these principles into local policy, communities can work towards creating a more just and sustainable future for all residents.

#### 7.1b Environmental Inequalities and Disparities

Environmental inequalities and disparities refer to the uneven distribution of environmental hazards and benefits among different communities. These inequalities are often linked to social, economic, and racial disparities, as marginalized and disadvantaged communities are disproportionately affected by environmental hazards and lack access to environmental benefits.

One of the most significant environmental inequalities in the United States is the issue of environmental racism. As discussed in the previous section, communities of color are more likely to be located next to pollution sources and have poor access to clean air and water. This not only has negative impacts on their physical health, but also on their mental health and overall well-being.

In addition to physical health impacts, environmental inequalities can also have economic consequences. Empirical evidence suggests that environmental hazards negatively affect nearby property values, employment opportunities, and economic activities. This can further exacerbate existing economic disparities and create barriers to upward mobility for marginalized communities.

Furthermore, environmental inequalities can also have psychological impacts. Exposure to environmental hazards can cause psychological stress, which can have long-term effects on mental health and well-being. This is particularly concerning for marginalized communities that may already face significant social and economic stressors.

#### 7.1c Case Studies of Environmental Justice and Equity Planning in Local Communities

To further illustrate the importance and effectiveness of environmental justice and equity planning in local communities, let us examine two case studies: the City of Portland, Oregon and the City of Richmond, California.

The City of Portland, Oregon has been a leader in implementing environmental justice policies and initiatives. In 1991, the city passed a resolution declaring its commitment to environmental justice and equity. This was followed by the creation of the Environmental Justice and Equity Program in 1993, which aims to address environmental inequalities and disparities in the city. One of the key strategies used by the city is the incorporation of EJIAs into policy development, which helps to ensure that the potential impacts on marginalized communities are carefully considered and addressed.

The City of Richmond, California has also made significant strides in addressing environmental justice and equity issues. In 2010, the city passed the Green Jobs and Green Business Ordinance, which aims to create green jobs and promote sustainable businesses in the city. This ordinance also includes provisions for environmental justice, such as prioritizing the hiring of local residents and providing job training opportunities for disadvantaged communities. Additionally, the city has implemented a community-based participatory research approach to address environmental inequalities and disparities, which involves collaboration between community members, researchers, and policymakers.

These case studies demonstrate the importance of local policy in addressing environmental justice and equity issues. By incorporating tools such as EIAs and EJIAs, and prioritizing environmental justice in decision-making processes, communities can work towards creating a more just and sustainable future for all residents. 





### Section: 7.1 Environmental Justice & Equity Planning:

Environmental justice and equity planning are crucial components of creating a just and sustainable city. As discussed in the previous section, environmental racism and disparities in access to clean air and water have been well-documented in the United States. These injustices have significant impacts on the health and well-being of communities, particularly those that are already marginalized and disadvantaged.

#### 7.1a The Role of Environmental Justice and Equity Planning in Local Policy

Local policy plays a critical role in addressing environmental justice and equity issues. It is at the local level that policies can be tailored to the specific needs and characteristics of a community. This allows for a more targeted and effective approach to addressing environmental inequalities and disparities.

One of the key ways in which local policy can address environmental justice and equity is through the implementation of environmental impact assessments (EIAs). EIAs are a tool used to evaluate the potential environmental impacts of a proposed project or policy. They can help identify potential environmental hazards and inform decision-making processes to mitigate these impacts. By incorporating EIAs into local policy, communities can ensure that new developments and policies do not exacerbate existing environmental inequalities.

Another important aspect of local policy is the consideration of environmental justice in decision-making processes. This can be achieved through the inclusion of environmental justice impact assessments (EJIAs) in policy development. EJIAs are a more comprehensive version of EIAs that specifically focus on the potential environmental justice impacts of a proposed project or policy. By conducting EJIAs, communities can ensure that the potential impacts on marginalized and disadvantaged communities are carefully considered and addressed.

In addition to these tools, local policy can also play a role in promoting environmental justice and equity through the implementation of equitable and sustainable housing and transportation policies. These policies can help address the unequal distribution of environmental hazards and benefits, and promote healthier and more livable communities for all residents.

#### 7.1b The Role of Environmental Justice and Equity Planning in Local Policy

Local policy plays a crucial role in addressing environmental justice and equity issues. It is at the local level that policies can be tailored to the specific needs and characteristics of a community. This allows for a more targeted and effective approach to addressing environmental inequalities and disparities.

One of the key ways in which local policy can address environmental justice and equity is through the implementation of environmental impact assessments (EIAs). EIAs are a tool used to evaluate the potential environmental impacts of a proposed project or policy. They can help identify potential environmental hazards and inform decision-making processes to mitigate these impacts. By incorporating EIAs into local policy, communities can ensure that new developments and policies do not exacerbate existing environmental inequalities.

Another important aspect of local policy is the consideration of environmental justice in decision-making processes. This can be achieved through the inclusion of environmental justice impact assessments (EJIAs) in policy development. EJIAs are a more comprehensive version of EIAs that specifically focus on the potential environmental justice impacts of a proposed project or policy. By conducting EJIAs, communities can ensure that the potential impacts on marginalized and disadvantaged communities are carefully considered and addressed.

In addition to these tools, local policy can also play a role in promoting environmental justice and equity through the implementation of equitable and sustainable housing and transportation policies. These policies can help address the unequal distribution of environmental hazards and benefits, and promote healthier and more livable communities for all residents.

#### 7.1c Planning for Environmental Justice and Equity

Planning for environmental justice and equity is a crucial aspect of local policy-making. It involves considering the potential environmental impacts of proposed projects and policies on marginalized and disadvantaged communities. This can be achieved through the use of environmental justice impact assessments (EJIAs) and environmental impact assessments (EIAs).

EJIAs are a more comprehensive version of EIAs that specifically focus on the potential environmental justice impacts of a proposed project or policy. They take into account the potential impacts on marginalized and disadvantaged communities, and provide recommendations for mitigating any potential negative impacts. By conducting EJIAs, communities can ensure that the potential impacts on marginalized and disadvantaged communities are carefully considered and addressed.

In addition to EJIAs, local policy can also incorporate equitable and sustainable housing and transportation policies. These policies can help address the unequal distribution of environmental hazards and benefits, and promote healthier and more livable communities for all residents. By considering the potential environmental impacts of proposed projects and policies on marginalized and disadvantaged communities, local policy can work towards creating a more just and sustainable city for all.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of environmental justice and equity planning in the context of local policy-driven strategies for economic development and the just city. We have discussed the importance of considering the environmental impacts of development policies and how they can disproportionately affect marginalized communities. We have also examined the role of equity planning in addressing these issues and promoting fair and just outcomes for all members of the community.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to development that takes into account both economic and environmental factors. This requires a shift away from traditional approaches that prioritize economic growth at all costs, and instead focuses on creating a balance between economic development and environmental sustainability. By incorporating equity planning into this holistic approach, we can ensure that marginalized communities are not further marginalized by development policies.

Another important aspect of environmental justice and equity planning is the role of community engagement. As we have seen, marginalized communities are often the most affected by development policies, yet their voices are often not heard in the decision-making process. By involving these communities in the planning and implementation of development policies, we can ensure that their needs and concerns are taken into account, leading to more equitable and just outcomes.

In conclusion, environmental justice and equity planning are crucial components of creating a just city. By incorporating these principles into local policy-driven strategies for economic development, we can create more sustainable and equitable communities for all members of the community.

## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

### Introduction

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become a crucial aspect of economic development and creating a just city. Equity and inclusion refer to the fair distribution of resources, opportunities, and benefits among all members of a society, regardless of their background or circumstances. This includes access to education, employment, healthcare, and other essential services. In the context of economic development, equity and inclusion are essential for creating a thriving and sustainable community. It is also crucial for promoting social cohesion and reducing inequalities.

In this chapter, we will explore the relationship between equity and inclusion and their impact on economic development. We will also discuss the role of local policies in promoting equity and inclusion and how they can be used to create a just city. This chapter will provide a comprehensive overview of the various strategies and initiatives that can be implemented at the local level to address issues of equity and inclusion. We will also examine the challenges and opportunities that arise in the process of creating a more equitable and inclusive society.

The chapter will begin by defining equity and inclusion and their significance in the context of economic development. We will then delve into the current state of equity and inclusion in the United States and the disparities that exist among different communities. This will provide a foundation for understanding the need for local policies and strategies to address these issues. We will also explore the various factors that contribute to inequities and exclusion, such as race, ethnicity, gender, and socioeconomic status.

Next, we will discuss the role of local policies in promoting equity and inclusion. This will include an examination of different types of policies, such as affirmative action, equal opportunity, and anti-discrimination laws. We will also explore the effectiveness of these policies and their impact on creating a more equitable and inclusive society. Additionally, we will discuss the challenges and limitations of local policies and how they can be addressed.

Finally, we will look at real-world examples of local policies and strategies that have been successful in promoting equity and inclusion. This will include case studies from different cities and communities, highlighting the innovative and effective approaches that have been implemented. We will also discuss the lessons learned from these examples and how they can be applied to other communities.

In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of equity and inclusion and their role in economic development. It will also serve as a guide for local policymakers and community leaders in creating a more equitable and inclusive society. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complex issues surrounding equity and inclusion and the importance of local policies in addressing them.

In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of environmental justice and equity planning in the context of local policy-driven strategies for economic development and the just city. We have discussed the importance of considering the environmental impacts of development policies and how they can disproportionately affect marginalized communities. We have also examined the role of equity planning in addressing these issues and promoting fair and just outcomes for all members of the community.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to development that takes into account both economic and environmental factors. This requires a shift away from traditional approaches that prioritize economic growth at all costs, and instead focuses on creating a balance between economic development and environmental sustainability. By incorporating equity planning into this holistic approach, we can ensure that marginalized communities are not further marginalized by development policies.

Another important aspect of environmental justice and equity planning is the role of community engagement. As we have seen, marginalized communities are often the most affected by development policies, yet their voices are often not heard in the decision-making process. By involving these communities in the planning and implementation of development policies, we can ensure that their needs and concerns are taken into account, leading to more equitable and just outcomes.

In conclusion, environmental justice and equity planning are crucial components of creating a just city. By incorporating these principles into local policy-driven strategies for economic development, we can create more sustainable and equitable communities for all members of the community.

## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

### Introduction

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become a crucial aspect of economic development and creating a just city. Equity and inclusion refer to the fair distribution of resources, opportunities, and benefits among all members of a society, regardless of their background or circumstances. This includes access to education, employment, healthcare, and other essential services. In the context of economic development, equity and inclusion are essential for creating a thriving and sustainable community. It is also crucial for promoting social cohesion and reducing inequalities.

In this chapter, we will explore the relationship between equity and inclusion and their impact on economic development. We will also discuss the role of local policies in promoting equity and inclusion and how they can be used to create a just city. This chapter will provide a comprehensive overview of the various strategies and initiatives that can be implemented at the local level to address issues of equity and inclusion. We will also examine the challenges and opportunities that arise in the process of creating a more equitable and inclusive society.

The chapter will begin by defining equity and inclusion and their significance in the context of economic development. We will then delve into the current state of equity and inclusion in the United States and the disparities that exist among different communities. This will provide a foundation for understanding the need for local policies and strategies to address these issues. We will also explore the various factors that contribute to inequities and exclusion, such as race, ethnicity, gender, and socioeconomic status.

Next, we will discuss the role of local policies in promoting equity and inclusion. This will include an examination of different types of policies, such as affirmative action, equal opportunity, and anti-discrimination laws. We will also explore the effectiveness of these policies and their impact on creating a more equitable and inclusive society. Additionally, we will discuss the challenges and limitations of local policies and how they can be addressed.

Finally, we will look at real-world examples of local policies and strategies that have been successful in promoting equity and inclusion. This will include case studies from different cities and communities, highlighting the innovative and effective approaches that have been implemented. We will also discuss the lessons learned from these examples and how they can be applied to other communities.

In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of equity and inclusion and their role in economic development. It will also serve as a guide for local policymakers and community leaders in creating a more equitable and inclusive society. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complex issues surrounding equity and inclusion and the importance of local policies in addressing them. 


## Chapter 8: Equity & Inclusion in Economic Development:




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the intersection of cultural heritage and preservation in the context of equity and inclusion. Cultural heritage and preservation are crucial components of a just city, as they contribute to the sense of identity and belonging for individuals and communities. They also play a significant role in economic development, as they attract tourists and create job opportunities.

We will begin by defining cultural heritage and preservation, and discussing their importance in promoting equity and inclusion. We will then delve into the various policies and strategies that can be implemented at the local level to protect and promote cultural heritage and preservation. This will include policies related to land use, zoning, and tax incentives, as well as strategies for community engagement and education.

Furthermore, we will examine case studies of successful cultural heritage and preservation initiatives in different cities around the world. These examples will provide valuable insights into the challenges and opportunities that come with implementing such policies and strategies.

Finally, we will discuss the potential benefits and drawbacks of cultural heritage and preservation in terms of equity and inclusion. We will also explore ways to address any potential conflicts that may arise between preserving cultural heritage and promoting economic development.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the role of cultural heritage and preservation in promoting equity and inclusion, and how local policies can be used to achieve these goals. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complexities and importance of cultural heritage and preservation in creating a just city.




### Subsection: 8.1a Importance of Cultural Heritage

Cultural heritage is a fundamental aspect of a just city, as it plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion. It is the tangible and intangible legacy of a community's history, traditions, and values, and serves as a source of identity and belonging for individuals and communities. In this section, we will explore the importance of cultural heritage in promoting equity and inclusion, and how it contributes to the overall well-being of a community.

#### The Role of Cultural Heritage in Promoting Equity

Cultural heritage is a powerful tool for promoting equity in a just city. It provides a sense of belonging and identity for marginalized communities, who may have been excluded or marginalized in the past. By preserving and promoting cultural heritage, we can create a more inclusive and equitable society, where all communities have a voice and are valued.

Moreover, cultural heritage can also serve as a source of economic opportunities for marginalized communities. By preserving and promoting traditional crafts, art forms, and cultural practices, we can create job opportunities and stimulate economic growth in these communities. This not only promotes equity, but also helps to reduce poverty and improve the overall well-being of these communities.

#### The Role of Cultural Heritage in Promoting Inclusion

Cultural heritage also plays a crucial role in promoting inclusion in a just city. It allows for the expression and celebration of diverse cultural identities, which is essential for creating a sense of belonging and acceptance for all individuals. By preserving and promoting cultural heritage, we can create a more inclusive and diverse community, where all individuals are valued and respected.

Furthermore, cultural heritage can also serve as a bridge between different communities, promoting understanding and acceptance. By learning about and celebrating the cultural heritage of others, we can break down barriers and promote inclusivity in our communities.

#### The Role of Cultural Heritage in Economic Development

Cultural heritage is not only important for promoting equity and inclusion, but also plays a significant role in economic development. It attracts tourists and creates job opportunities, contributing to the overall economic growth of a city. By preserving and promoting cultural heritage, we can create a unique and attractive destination for tourists, stimulating economic growth and creating job opportunities.

Moreover, cultural heritage can also serve as a source of innovation and creativity, driving economic development. By preserving and promoting traditional crafts, art forms, and cultural practices, we can inspire new ideas and innovations, leading to the development of new industries and job opportunities.

In conclusion, cultural heritage is a crucial aspect of a just city, promoting equity, inclusion, and economic development. By preserving and promoting cultural heritage, we can create a more inclusive and equitable society, where all communities have a voice and are valued. It also serves as a source of economic opportunities and innovation, driving economic growth and creating job opportunities. In the next section, we will explore the various policies and strategies that can be implemented at the local level to protect and promote cultural heritage and preservation.





### Subsection: 8.1b Preservation Planning and Policies

Preservation planning and policies are crucial for the protection and promotion of cultural heritage. They provide a framework for decision-making and action, ensuring that cultural heritage is preserved and promoted in a systematic and equitable manner. In this section, we will explore the principles and strategies for preservation planning and policies, and how they contribute to the overall goal of promoting equity and inclusion through cultural heritage.

#### Principles for Preservation Planning and Policies

The principles for preservation planning and policies are based on the concept of sustainability, which involves meeting the needs of the present without compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs. In the context of cultural heritage, this means preserving and promoting cultural heritage in a way that is respectful of the past, responsive to the present, and sustainable for the future.

The principles for preservation planning and policies also include the principles of equity and inclusion. This means ensuring that all communities have a voice in the decision-making process and that their cultural heritage is valued and respected. It also means promoting diversity and inclusivity in the preservation and promotion of cultural heritage.

#### Strategies for Preservation Planning and Policies

There are several strategies that can be used for preservation planning and policies. These include:

- **Inventory and Assessment:** This involves identifying and documenting cultural heritage resources, assessing their significance, and prioritizing their preservation.
- **Preservation Planning:** This involves developing a plan for the preservation of cultural heritage resources, including strategies for protection, conservation, and interpretation.
- **Policy Development:** This involves creating policies and guidelines for the preservation and promotion of cultural heritage, including regulations for development and alterations to historic buildings and sites.
- **Community Engagement:** This involves involving local communities in the preservation planning and decision-making process, ensuring that their cultural heritage is valued and respected.
- **Education and Outreach:** This involves educating the public about the importance of cultural heritage and promoting understanding and appreciation for diverse cultural traditions and practices.
- **Partnerships and Collaborations:** This involves working with other organizations and stakeholders to preserve and promote cultural heritage, including government agencies, non-profit organizations, and private sector entities.

#### Case Studies of Preservation Planning and Policies

To further illustrate the principles and strategies for preservation planning and policies, let's look at some case studies.

- **The Historic District of Old Québec:** The Historic District of Old Québec is a UNESCO World Heritage site that has been preserved through a combination of inventory and assessment, preservation planning, and policy development. The city has also engaged in community engagement and education efforts to promote understanding and appreciation for the district's cultural heritage.
- **The National Trust for Historic Preservation:** The National Trust for Historic Preservation is a non-profit organization that works to preserve and promote historic places across the United States. They use a variety of strategies, including inventory and assessment, preservation planning, and policy development, to protect and promote cultural heritage.
- **The Smithsonian Institution:** The Smithsonian Institution is a museum and research complex that has a strong commitment to preserving and promoting cultural heritage. They use a combination of inventory and assessment, preservation planning, and policy development, as well as education and outreach, to fulfill this commitment.

In conclusion, preservation planning and policies are essential for promoting equity and inclusion through cultural heritage. By following the principles of sustainability, equity, and inclusion, and implementing strategies such as inventory and assessment, preservation planning, and policy development, we can ensure that cultural heritage is preserved and promoted in a systematic and equitable manner.




### Subsection: 8.1c Balancing Development and Preservation

Balancing development and preservation is a critical aspect of cultural heritage and preservation. As cities and communities continue to grow and evolve, there is often a tension between the need for development and the desire to preserve cultural heritage resources. This section will explore strategies for balancing development and preservation, and how they can be used to promote equity and inclusion in the preservation of cultural heritage.

#### Strategies for Balancing Development and Preservation

There are several strategies that can be used to balance development and preservation. These include:

- **Preservation by Design:** This involves incorporating preservation considerations into the design and planning process for new developments. This can include incorporating historic buildings or features into new developments, or designing new developments in a way that respects and complements existing cultural heritage resources.
- **Preservation Easements:** Preservation easements are legal agreements that restrict the use of a property in order to protect its cultural heritage resources. They can be used to protect specific features or entire properties, and can be used in conjunction with other preservation strategies.
- **Adaptive Reuse:** Adaptive reuse involves repurposing existing buildings for new uses. This can be a cost-effective and sustainable way to preserve cultural heritage resources, while also meeting the needs of the community.
- **Preservation Funding:** Preservation funding can be used to support the preservation of cultural heritage resources. This can include grants for preservation projects, tax incentives for preservation efforts, or public-private partnerships to fund preservation initiatives.
- **Public Education and Engagement:** Public education and engagement can help to raise awareness and understanding of the importance of preserving cultural heritage. This can include community workshops, public talks, and educational programs that highlight the value of cultural heritage and the need for its preservation.

#### Case Studies of Balancing Development and Preservation

To further illustrate these strategies, let's look at some case studies of successful balancing of development and preservation.

- **The High Line, New York City:** The High Line is a 1.45-mile-long elevated linear park built on a former freight rail line in New York City. The project involved the adaptive reuse of an abandoned railway line, preserving a unique piece of the city's history while also creating a new public space for the community.
- **The American Tobacco Historic District, Durham, North Carolina:** The American Tobacco Historic District is a 10-block historic district that has been revitalized through a combination of preservation and new development. The project involved the preservation of several historic buildings, as well as the construction of new buildings that respect the character of the district.
- **The Preservation of the Old Metropolis, Veria, Greece:** The Old Metropolis of Veria is a historic district in northern Greece that has been preserved through a combination of preservation easements and adaptive reuse. The project involved the protection of the district's historic buildings and the adaptive reuse of several buildings for new uses, such as shops and restaurants.

These case studies demonstrate the potential for balancing development and preservation in a way that promotes equity and inclusion in the preservation of cultural heritage. By incorporating these strategies into local policies and planning processes, we can ensure the preservation of our cultural heritage for future generations.





#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the importance of cultural heritage and preservation in the context of equity and inclusion. We have discussed how cultural heritage is a reflection of a community's identity and how it can be used as a tool for economic development and creating a just city. We have also examined the role of preservation in protecting and promoting cultural heritage, and how it can contribute to creating a sense of place and belonging for all members of a community.

Cultural heritage and preservation are not just about preserving physical structures or artifacts. They are also about preserving the intangible aspects of a community's identity, such as traditions, customs, and values. By preserving these aspects, we can create a sense of pride and belonging among community members, which is essential for creating a just and inclusive city.

Moreover, we have discussed how cultural heritage and preservation can be used as a tool for economic development. By promoting cultural tourism and creating opportunities for local businesses to showcase their cultural heritage, we can create job opportunities and stimulate the local economy. This not only benefits the community economically but also promotes a sense of ownership and pride among community members.

In conclusion, cultural heritage and preservation play a crucial role in creating a just and inclusive city. By recognizing and promoting cultural heritage, we can create a sense of place and belonging for all members of a community, while also promoting economic development and creating job opportunities. It is essential for local governments to have policies in place that prioritize and protect cultural heritage and preservation, as it contributes to creating a more equitable and inclusive society.
