## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City

### Introduction:

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become increasingly important in shaping the future of our cities. As urban populations continue to grow, it is crucial for policymakers to consider the needs and perspectives of all members of the community, especially those who have been historically marginalized or excluded. This is where the role of local policy becomes crucial. Local policies have the power to shape the economic development of a city, and when implemented with a focus on equity and inclusion, can create a more just and sustainable future for all.

In this chapter, we will explore the various ways in which local policies can be used to promote equity and inclusion in economic development. We will discuss the importance of understanding the historical and social context of a city, as well as the role of community engagement and participation in policy-making. Additionally, we will examine the impact of different policies on different groups, and how to ensure that these policies are equitable and inclusive.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the role of local policy in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development. By the end, readers will have a better understanding of the complexities of this topic and be equipped with the knowledge and tools to implement policies that promote equity and inclusion in their own communities. 





### Section: 16.1 Transportation Planning and Equity:

Transportation planning is a critical aspect of urban development that has a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of a city. It is the process of determining the transportation needs of a community and developing strategies to meet those needs. However, traditional transportation planning has often been criticized for its lack of consideration for the needs and interests of marginalized communities. This has resulted in transportation systems that are not equitable, inclusive, and just.

#### 16.1a The Role of Transportation in Urban Equity

Transportation is a fundamental aspect of urban life. It is the means by which people and goods move around a city, connecting different neighborhoods, job opportunities, and services. However, not all members of a community have equal access to transportation. Marginalized communities, such as low-income residents, people of color, and immigrants, often face barriers to accessing transportation, leading to transportation inequality.

Transportation inequality is a result of systemic discrimination and exclusion in transportation planning and decision-making processes. For example, in many urban centers, minority areas are often overlooked in transportation planning, resulting in inadequate transportation options. This can lead to overcrowded and unsafe transportation routes, making it difficult for residents to access essential services and opportunities.

Moreover, marginalized communities are often more reliant on public transportation, as they may not have access to private vehicles. This further exacerbates transportation inequality, as these communities are more vulnerable to changes in transportation policies and services. For instance, the implementation of anti-sprawl policies, such as urban intensification, can increase housing prices, making it more difficult for low-income residents to afford housing in urban areas.

To address transportation inequality, it is essential to incorporate equity and inclusion into transportation planning. This involves considering the needs and interests of marginalized communities in decision-making processes and developing strategies that promote equitable access to transportation. One way to achieve this is through the use of transportation demand management (TDM) strategies.

#### 16.1b Transportation Demand Management and Equity

Transportation demand management (TDM) is a set of strategies aimed at reducing the demand for single-occupancy vehicles (SOVs) and promoting the use of more sustainable modes of transportation. These strategies can help address transportation inequality by providing more equitable access to transportation options for marginalized communities.

TDM strategies can be implemented at the local, regional, and national levels. At the local level, TDM can be used to address transportation inequality by promoting the use of public transportation, walking, and biking. This can be achieved through the implementation of policies such as transit-oriented development, complete streets, and congestion pricing. These strategies can help improve access to transportation for marginalized communities and reduce the reliance on private vehicles.

At the regional and national levels, TDM can be used to address transportation inequality by promoting the use of sustainable modes of transportation, such as electric vehicles and autonomous vehicles. These technologies can help reduce the cost of transportation for marginalized communities and improve access to transportation options. Additionally, policies such as fuel efficiency standards and alternative fuel incentives can also help address transportation inequality by reducing the cost of transportation for all communities.

In conclusion, transportation planning plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in a city. By incorporating equity and inclusion into transportation planning and implementing TDM strategies, we can help address transportation inequality and create a more just and equitable transportation system for all members of a community. 





#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the critical role of transportation planning in promoting equity and inclusion in urban areas. We have discussed how transportation planning can impact access to opportunities, such as jobs, education, and healthcare, and how it can contribute to the creation of a just city. We have also examined the various factors that must be considered in transportation planning, including the needs and preferences of different communities, the potential impacts on the environment, and the integration with other urban planning efforts.

Transportation planning is a complex and multifaceted process that requires careful consideration of a wide range of factors. It is also a highly political process, with decisions often influenced by competing interests and ideologies. However, by adopting a policy-driven approach, local governments can ensure that transportation planning is guided by a clear set of principles and objectives that promote equity and inclusion.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of involving all stakeholders in the transportation planning process. This includes not only those directly affected by transportation decisions, but also those who may be impacted indirectly, such as businesses and environmental groups. By engaging in a transparent and inclusive planning process, local governments can ensure that the needs and concerns of all stakeholders are taken into account.

Another important aspect of transportation planning is the consideration of equity and inclusion in decision-making. This means not only ensuring that all communities have equal access to transportation services, but also that their voices are heard in the planning process. By promoting equity and inclusion in transportation planning, local governments can help create a more just and equitable city for all its residents.

In conclusion, transportation planning plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in urban areas. By adopting a policy-driven approach and involving all stakeholders in the planning process, local governments can ensure that transportation decisions are guided by a commitment to equity and inclusion. This not only benefits the individuals and communities directly affected, but also contributes to the creation of a more just and sustainable city for all.

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 17: Local Policies:




### Introduction

Urban design plays a crucial role in shaping the physical environment of cities, and it has a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of its residents. This chapter will explore the relationship between urban design and equity, and how local policies can be used to promote equitable and inclusive urban design.

Urban design is the process of shaping the physical features of a city, such as its streets, buildings, and public spaces, to create a functional and aesthetically pleasing environment. It involves a range of disciplines, including architecture, landscape architecture, urban planning, and engineering. The goal of urban design is to create a city that is safe, accessible, and enjoyable for all its residents, regardless of their socio-economic status, race, or ability.

However, the reality is that many cities are not designed with equity and inclusion in mind. The physical environment of a city can perpetuate social and economic inequalities, making it difficult for certain groups to access opportunities and resources. For example, a city with a lack of affordable housing options may limit the ability of low-income residents to find suitable housing, leading to housing insecurity and other social and economic challenges.

Local policies can play a crucial role in promoting equitable and inclusive urban design. These policies can set guidelines and regulations for development projects, ensuring that they are designed and implemented in a way that promotes equity and inclusion. They can also provide incentives for developers to incorporate equity and inclusion principles into their projects.

In this chapter, we will explore the various ways in which local policies can be used to promote equitable and inclusive urban design. We will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that arise when implementing these policies, and how they can be addressed. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the role of urban design in promoting equity and inclusion, and the strategies that can be used to create more equitable and inclusive cities.




### Subsection: 17.1a Understanding Urban Design

Urban design is a multidisciplinary field that combines elements of architecture, landscape architecture, and urban planning to create functional and aesthetically pleasing cities. It is a crucial aspect of urban development, as it shapes the physical environment of a city and has a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of its residents.

#### The Role of Urban Design in Equity and Inclusion

Urban design plays a critical role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. The physical environment of a city can perpetuate social and economic inequalities, making it difficult for certain groups to access opportunities and resources. For example, a city with a lack of affordable housing options may limit the ability of low-income residents to find suitable housing, leading to housing insecurity and other social and economic challenges.

On the other hand, urban design can also be used as a tool to promote equity and inclusion. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion into the design of a city, we can create a physical environment that is safe, accessible, and enjoyable for all residents, regardless of their socio-economic status, race, or ability.

#### The Role of Local Policies in Promoting Equitable and Inclusive Urban Design

Local policies play a crucial role in promoting equitable and inclusive urban design. These policies can set guidelines and regulations for development projects, ensuring that they are designed and implemented in a way that promotes equity and inclusion. They can also provide incentives for developers to incorporate equity and inclusion principles into their projects.

For example, a local policy could require that a certain percentage of affordable housing units be included in any new development project. This would help address the issue of housing affordability and ensure that low-income residents have access to suitable housing options.

#### The Challenges and Opportunities of Implementing Equity and Inclusion Principles in Urban Design

While incorporating equity and inclusion principles into urban design can be challenging, it also presents many opportunities. By promoting equity and inclusion, we can create a more just and equitable city for all residents. This can lead to improved quality of life, increased community engagement, and a stronger sense of belonging for all residents.

However, there are also challenges that must be addressed when implementing equity and inclusion principles in urban design. These include limited resources, competing interests, and the need for collaboration and communication among various stakeholders.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, urban design plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. Local policies can be used as a tool to incorporate equity and inclusion principles into the design of a city, creating a physical environment that is safe, accessible, and enjoyable for all residents. While there are challenges to implementing these principles, the opportunities for creating a more just and equitable city make it a worthwhile endeavor. 





### Subsection: 17.1b The Role of Design in Urban Equity

Urban design plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. It is the process of shaping the physical environment of a city to meet the needs and desires of its residents. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion into urban design, we can create a physical environment that is safe, accessible, and enjoyable for all residents, regardless of their socio-economic status, race, or ability.

#### The Role of Design in Promoting Equity and Inclusion

Design is a powerful tool for promoting equity and inclusion in cities. It has the ability to shape the physical environment in a way that addresses social and economic inequalities. For example, a well-designed public space can provide a safe and accessible place for all residents to gather and interact, promoting social inclusion. Similarly, a well-designed transportation system can improve accessibility and reduce transportation barriers for marginalized communities.

#### The Role of Local Policies in Promoting Equitable and Inclusive Design

Local policies play a crucial role in promoting equitable and inclusive design. These policies can set guidelines and regulations for design projects, ensuring that they are designed and implemented in a way that promotes equity and inclusion. They can also provide incentives for designers to incorporate equity and inclusion principles into their projects.

For example, a local policy could require that all public spaces be designed with universal design principles in mind, ensuring that they are accessible to all residents, regardless of their ability. This would promote inclusion and reduce barriers for marginalized communities.

#### The Challenges and Opportunities of Design in Urban Equity

While design has the potential to promote equity and inclusion, it also presents some challenges. One of the main challenges is the potential for gentrification and displacement. As cities become more desirable and attractive, there is a risk of rising property values and rents, leading to displacement of low-income residents. This can exacerbate existing social and economic inequalities.

However, design also presents opportunities for promoting equity and inclusion. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion into the design of a city, we can create a more just and equitable society for all residents. This requires a collaborative and inclusive approach to design, where all voices are heard and considered.

In conclusion, design plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion into the design of a city, we can create a physical environment that is safe, accessible, and enjoyable for all residents. Local policies can support and guide this process, ensuring that design promotes equity and inclusion in a just and equitable manner.





### Subsection: 17.1c Strategies for Equitable Urban Design

Urban design is a powerful tool for promoting equity and inclusion in cities. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion into urban design, we can create a physical environment that is safe, accessible, and enjoyable for all residents, regardless of their socio-economic status, race, or ability. In this section, we will explore some strategies for equitable urban design.

#### Universal Design

Universal design is a design approach that aims to create products and environments that are usable by all people, to the greatest extent possible, without the need for adaptation or specialized design. This approach is particularly relevant in urban design, as it can help to create a physical environment that is accessible to all residents, regardless of their ability. By incorporating universal design principles into urban design, we can create a more inclusive city.

#### Inclusive Public Spaces

Public spaces, such as parks, plazas, and sidewalks, are an important part of urban design. They provide opportunities for residents to gather, interact, and enjoy the city. By designing these spaces with inclusivity in mind, we can create a more equitable city. This can be achieved by incorporating features such as ramps, seating areas, and accessible pathways, as well as designing spaces that are safe and comfortable for all residents.

#### Equitable Transportation Systems

Transportation is a crucial aspect of urban design. It can have a significant impact on the equity and inclusion of a city. By designing transportation systems with equity and inclusion in mind, we can create a more equitable city. This can be achieved by incorporating features such as accessible public transportation, safe and accessible pedestrian and cycling infrastructure, and equitable distribution of transportation services.

#### Community Engagement

Community engagement is a crucial aspect of equitable urban design. By involving community members in the design process, we can ensure that their needs and desires are taken into account. This can help to create a more inclusive and equitable city, as community members can provide valuable insights and feedback on the design of their city.

#### Equity-Driven Policies and Regulations

Local policies and regulations play a crucial role in promoting equitable urban design. By setting guidelines and regulations that prioritize equity and inclusion, we can ensure that urban design projects are designed and implemented in a way that promotes equity and inclusion. This can include policies and regulations that require universal design, promote inclusive public spaces, and prioritize equitable transportation systems.

In conclusion, equitable urban design is crucial for creating a just city. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion into urban design, we can create a physical environment that is safe, accessible, and enjoyable for all residents. This can be achieved through strategies such as universal design, inclusive public spaces, equitable transportation systems, community engagement, and equity-driven policies and regulations. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the important role of urban design in promoting equity and inclusion in cities. We have discussed how urban design can shape the physical environment and create opportunities for marginalized communities to participate in the decision-making process. We have also examined the various strategies and policies that can be implemented to promote equitable and inclusive urban design, such as community engagement, diversity in design teams, and affordable housing.

It is clear that urban design plays a crucial role in creating a just city. By incorporating principles of equity and inclusion into the design process, we can create more inclusive and equitable communities. This not only benefits marginalized communities, but also contributes to the overall well-being and livability of the city.

As we continue to develop and shape our cities, it is important to prioritize equity and inclusion in urban design. By doing so, we can create more just and livable cities for all residents.

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of a just city has become increasingly important. This is especially true in the context of economic development, where the distribution of resources and opportunities can greatly impact the well-being of different communities within a city.

In this chapter, we will explore the relationship between urban planning and equity, and how local policies can be used to promote a more just and inclusive city. We will examine the various factors that contribute to economic inequality, such as race, class, and gender, and how they intersect with urban planning decisions. We will also discuss the role of community engagement and participation in the planning process, and how it can lead to more equitable outcomes.

We will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that arise when trying to create a just city, and the role of equity and inclusion in achieving a more sustainable and livable future for all.

By examining the various factors that contribute to economic inequality and exploring the principles of a just city, we can work towards creating more equitable and sustainable communities for all.

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 18: Equity and Inclusion in Economic Development:




### Introduction

Land use planning is a critical component of urban development and management. It involves the systematic organization and management of land resources to meet the needs of a community. This chapter will explore the relationship between land use planning and equity, and how local policies can be used to promote economic development and create a just city.

Land use planning is a complex process that involves multiple stakeholders, including government agencies, developers, and community members. It is a tool for shaping the physical form of a city, influencing the distribution of resources, and promoting social and economic equity. However, the process is not without its challenges. Land use planning can be a contentious issue, with competing interests and values often at play.

In this chapter, we will delve into the various aspects of land use planning, including zoning, density, and transportation planning. We will also examine how these elements can be used to promote equity and inclusion in a city. The chapter will also explore the role of local policies in shaping land use planning decisions and how these policies can be used to address issues of equity and inclusion.

The goal of this chapter is to provide a comprehensive understanding of the relationship between land use planning and equity. By the end of this chapter, readers should have a better understanding of the role of land use planning in creating a just city and the strategies that can be used to promote equity and inclusion in urban development.




### Subsection: 18.1a Understanding Land Use Planning

Land use planning is a crucial aspect of urban development and management. It involves the systematic organization and management of land resources to meet the needs of a community. This process is guided by local policies and regulations, and it plays a significant role in promoting equity and inclusion in a city.

#### The Role of Land Use Planning in Promoting Equity and Inclusion

Land use planning is a powerful tool for promoting equity and inclusion in a city. It allows for the systematic allocation of resources and the shaping of the physical form of a city in a way that addresses the needs and concerns of all members of the community. By involving all stakeholders in the planning process, land use planning can help to create a sense of ownership and belonging, which is crucial for promoting equity and inclusion.

Moreover, land use planning can help to address issues of spatial justice. Spatial justice refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities across different spatial units, such as neighborhoods or districts. By considering the spatial dimensions of equity and inclusion, land use planning can help to create more equitable and inclusive cities.

#### The Importance of Technology in Land Use Planning

Technology plays a crucial role in land use planning. Online land planning, for instance, allows for the effective use of the internet to support information sharing and decision making from remote locations. This approach can be particularly beneficial for property owners, communities, businesses, and government agencies that have limited access, time, finances, or personnel to make informed decisions about land use.

The use of the Internet, coupled with software technology such as geographic information systems (GIS), allows municipalities and other public and private organizations to compile base information, exchange information, present solutions to land planning issues, and receive feedback. This approach can help to streamline the land use planning process and make it more accessible to all members of the community.

#### The Role of Local Policies in Shaping Land Use Planning Decisions

Local policies play a crucial role in shaping land use planning decisions. These policies are often guided by the principles of equity and inclusion, and they provide a framework for addressing the needs and concerns of all members of the community. By promoting equity and inclusion, local policies can help to create a just city where all members have equal access to resources and opportunities.

In the next section, we will delve deeper into the various aspects of land use planning, including zoning, density, and transportation planning. We will also explore how these elements can be used to promote equity and inclusion in a city.





### Subsection: 18.1b The Role of Land Use in Urban Equity

Land use planning plays a pivotal role in promoting urban equity. It is through this process that cities can ensure that all residents, regardless of their socio-economic status, have access to quality housing, education, healthcare, and employment opportunities. This section will delve into the role of land use in urban equity, focusing on the concept of urban sprawl and its impact on transportation inequality.

#### Urban Sprawl and Transportation Inequality

Urban sprawl, characterized by the uncontrolled expansion of urban areas into surrounding rural or undeveloped land, has been a major concern in many cities across the United States. This phenomenon has been linked to a range of negative social, economic, and environmental impacts, including transportation inequality.

Critics of urban sprawl argue that it exacerbates transportation inequality by limiting access to transportation options for minority groups. In many urban centers, such as Los Angeles and San Francisco, transportation in minority areas is often lacking, leading to overcrowded and unsafe transportation routes that do not provide a comprehensive means of transportation. This disparity is further exacerbated because minority residents are more reliant on public transportation.

#### The Paradox of Intensification

The concept of the paradox of intensification, as proposed by Melia et al. (2011), is also relevant to the discussion of urban equity. This paradox suggests that while planning policies that increase population densities in urban areas can reduce car use, the effect is weak, and thus, doubling the population density of a particular area will not halve the frequency or distance of car use. This finding highlights the need for a more nuanced approach to land use planning that takes into account the complex interplay between population density, transportation options, and urban equity.

#### Risk of Increased Housing Prices

While land use planning can play a crucial role in promoting urban equity, there is also a concern that anti-sprawl policies may lead to increased housing prices. Some research suggests that this has been the case in cities like Portland, Oregon, where anti-sprawl policies have been implemented. However, other research shows that Portland's price increases are comparable to other Western cities, suggesting that the relationship between anti-sprawl policies and housing affordability is complex and requires further investigation.

In conclusion, land use planning plays a crucial role in promoting urban equity. However, it is important to consider the potential unintended consequences of land use policies, such as the risk of increased housing prices. By taking a comprehensive and inclusive approach to land use planning, cities can work towards creating more equitable and inclusive communities.




### Subsection: 18.1c Strategies for Equitable Land Use Planning

Equitable land use planning is a critical component of promoting urban equity. It involves the development of policies and strategies that ensure all residents, regardless of their socio-economic status, have equal access to quality housing, education, healthcare, and employment opportunities. This section will explore some strategies for equitable land use planning, focusing on the concept of transit-oriented development and its potential to address transportation inequality.

#### Transit-Oriented Development

Transit-oriented development (TOD) is a planning strategy that focuses on creating compact, walkable, and transit-friendly communities. The goal of TOD is to create communities where residents have access to a variety of transportation options, including public transit, walking, and biking. This strategy has been shown to be particularly effective in addressing transportation inequality.

TOD can help to address transportation inequality by providing residents with access to a variety of transportation options. This can be particularly beneficial for minority groups who are often more reliant on public transportation. By creating communities where public transportation is convenient and accessible, TOD can help to reduce transportation barriers and improve equity.

#### The Role of Policy

Policy plays a crucial role in promoting equitable land use planning. Policies can be used to guide development in a way that promotes equity. For example, policies can be put in place to encourage the development of affordable housing in areas with good transit access. This can help to ensure that low-income residents have access to quality housing in areas with good transportation options.

Policies can also be used to promote equitable land use planning by requiring developers to include a certain percentage of affordable housing units in new developments. This can help to address the issue of housing affordability, which is a major factor in urban equity.

#### The Importance of Community Engagement

Community engagement is another important strategy for equitable land use planning. By involving community members in the planning process, planners can ensure that the needs and concerns of all residents are taken into account. This can help to promote equity by ensuring that the planning process is inclusive and participatory.

Community engagement can also help to address issues of transportation inequality. By involving community members in the planning process, planners can ensure that the needs and concerns of all residents, including those who are reliant on public transportation, are taken into account. This can help to ensure that TOD strategies are implemented in a way that is equitable and beneficial for all residents.

In conclusion, equitable land use planning is a critical component of promoting urban equity. Strategies such as transit-oriented development, policy, and community engagement can all play a role in promoting equitable land use planning and addressing issues of transportation inequality. By implementing these strategies, cities can work towards creating more equitable and inclusive communities.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the critical role of land use planning in promoting equity and inclusion in urban development. We have seen how land use planning can be used as a tool to address issues of social, economic, and environmental inequality. By carefully planning the use of land, we can create more equitable and inclusive cities where all residents have access to quality housing, education, employment, and public services.

We have also discussed the importance of community engagement in land use planning. By involving community members in the planning process, we can ensure that their needs and concerns are taken into account, leading to more effective and sustainable solutions. This not only promotes equity and inclusion but also helps to build trust and ownership among community members, leading to a more cohesive and resilient community.

Finally, we have highlighted the role of policy in land use planning. Policies can provide a framework for decision-making and guide the implementation of land use plans. They can also help to address systemic issues of inequality and exclusion, such as gentrification and displacement. By incorporating equity and inclusion principles into policy, we can create a more just and sustainable urban future.

#### Exercise 2
Explain the importance of community engagement in land use planning. Discuss how involving community members in the planning process can lead to more effective and sustainable solutions.

#### Exercise 3

## Chapter: Chapter 19: Housing Policy and Equity

### Introduction

The concept of housing policy and equity is a critical aspect of urban development and the just city. This chapter delves into the intricate relationship between housing policies and their impact on equity, particularly in the context of local governance and economic development. 

Housing policy refers to the set of rules, regulations, and guidelines that govern the provision of housing in a particular area. These policies are often developed and implemented by local governments, and they play a crucial role in shaping the housing landscape of a city. They determine who can access housing, what type of housing is available, and at what cost. 

Equity, in the context of housing, refers to the fair distribution of housing opportunities and resources among different groups of people. It is about ensuring that everyone, regardless of their socio-economic status, race, or ethnicity, has access to safe, affordable, and decent housing. 

The intersection of housing policy and equity is complex and multifaceted. On one hand, housing policies can be used as a tool to promote equity by providing affordable housing options for low-income groups. On the other hand, they can also exacerbate existing inequalities if they are not carefully designed and implemented. 

This chapter will explore these issues in depth, providing a comprehensive overview of the role of housing policy in promoting equity and inclusion in urban development. It will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that local governments face in this regard, and propose strategies for developing more equitable housing policies.




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the critical role of land use planning in promoting equity and inclusion in our cities. We have discussed how land use planning can be used as a tool to address issues of economic development and create a just city for all residents. By examining the various factors that influence land use planning, such as zoning by-laws, density, and transportation, we have gained a deeper understanding of the complexities of this process.

We have also delved into the concept of equity and inclusion in land use planning, and how it can be achieved through policies that promote diversity, accessibility, and affordability. By incorporating these principles into land use planning, we can create more inclusive and equitable communities where all residents have equal access to opportunities and resources.

Furthermore, we have discussed the importance of community engagement and participation in land use planning. By involving all stakeholders, including marginalized and underrepresented groups, in the planning process, we can ensure that their needs and concerns are addressed, leading to more equitable and inclusive outcomes.

In conclusion, land use planning plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in our cities. By understanding the various factors that influence this process and incorporating principles of equity and inclusion, we can create more just and sustainable communities for all residents.

#### Exercise 2

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the critical role of land use planning in promoting equity and inclusion in our cities. We have discussed how land use planning can be used as a tool to address issues of economic development and create a just city for all residents. By examining the various factors that influence land use planning, such as zoning by-laws, density, and transportation, we have gained a deeper understanding of the complexities of this process.

We have also delved into the concept of equity and inclusion in land use planning, and how it can be achieved through policies that promote diversity, accessibility, and affordability. By incorporating these principles into land use planning, we can create more inclusive and equitable communities where all residents have equal access to opportunities and resources.

Furthermore, we have discussed the importance of community engagement and participation in land use planning. By involving all stakeholders, including marginalized and underrepresented groups, in the planning process, we can ensure that their needs and concerns are addressed, leading to more equitable and inclusive outcomes.

In conclusion, land use planning plays a crucial role in promoting equity and inclusion in our cities. By understanding the various factors that influence this process and incorporating principles of equity and inclusion, we can create more just and sustainable communities for all residents.

### Exercises

#### Exercise 1
Research and analyze a recent land use planning decision in your city or a nearby community. Discuss the potential impact of this decision on equity and inclusion in the community.

#### Exercise 2
Create a hypothetical land use plan for a diverse and inclusive community. Consider the principles of equity and inclusion in your plan and explain how they were incorporated.

#### Exercise 3

#### Exercise 4

#### Exercise 5

# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter 19: Local Policies and Equity:




### Introduction

Climate change is a global phenomenon that has far-reaching implications for urban areas. As the world's population continues to grow and more people move to cities, the impact of climate change on urban areas becomes increasingly significant. This chapter will explore the intersection of climate change and urban equity, examining how climate change exacerbates existing inequalities and how local policy-driven strategies can address these issues.

Climate change is expected to have profound effects on urban areas, including increased frequency and severity of extreme weather events, changes in precipitation patterns, and rising sea levels. These changes will disproportionately affect marginalized communities, who often live in areas that are more vulnerable to the impacts of climate change. This chapter will delve into the ways in which climate change exacerbates urban inequalities and the challenges this presents for local governments.

Local policy-driven strategies can play a crucial role in addressing the impacts of climate change on urban equity. These strategies can include policies that promote sustainable and resilient urban development, as well as initiatives that aim to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and mitigate the effects of climate change. This chapter will explore these strategies and their potential to create more equitable and sustainable urban areas.

In the following sections, we will delve deeper into the topic of climate change and urban equity, examining the current state of research and policy in this area. We will also explore case studies of cities around the world that are implementing innovative and effective strategies to address climate change and promote urban equity. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the complex relationship between climate change and urban equity, and the role that local policy-driven strategies can play in creating more equitable and sustainable urban areas.




### Subsection: 19.1a Understanding Climate Change Impacts on Cities

Climate change is a global phenomenon that has far-reaching implications for urban areas. As the world's population continues to grow and more people move to cities, the impact of climate change on urban areas becomes increasingly significant. This section will explore the intersection of climate change and urban equity, examining how climate change exacerbates existing inequalities and how local policy-driven strategies can address these issues.

Climate change is expected to have profound effects on urban areas, including increased frequency and severity of extreme weather events, changes in precipitation patterns, and rising sea levels. These changes will disproportionately affect marginalized communities, who often live in areas that are more vulnerable to the impacts of climate change. This section will delve into the ways in which climate change exacerbates urban inequalities and the challenges this presents for local governments.

Local policy-driven strategies can play a crucial role in addressing the impacts of climate change on urban equity. These strategies can include policies that promote sustainable and resilient urban development, as well as initiatives that aim to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and mitigate the effects of climate change. This section will explore these strategies and their potential to create more equitable and sustainable urban areas.

#### 19.1a.1 Climate Change Impacts on Urban Areas

Climate change is expected to have significant impacts on urban areas, particularly in terms of extreme weather events. As temperatures rise, the frequency and severity of heatwaves, droughts, and floods are expected to increase. These events can have devastating consequences for urban areas, particularly for marginalized communities who may lack the resources to mitigate these impacts.

Heatwaves, for example, can lead to increased mortality rates, particularly among vulnerable populations such as the elderly and young children. Droughts can also have severe consequences, leading to crop failures, water shortages, and increased competition for resources. Floods, on the other hand, can result in damage to infrastructure and displacement of communities.

#### 19.1a.2 Climate Change and Urban Inequalities

Climate change exacerbates existing inequalities in urban areas. Marginalized communities, who often live in areas that are more vulnerable to the impacts of climate change, are disproportionately affected by these events. This is due to a variety of factors, including their lack of access to resources and their often precarious living conditions.

For example, low-income communities may live in areas that are more prone to flooding due to their location near rivers or in informal settlements. When floods occur, these communities may lack the resources to evacuate or to rebuild after the event. Similarly, marginalized communities may lack access to air conditioning or other means of cooling during heatwaves, increasing their vulnerability to these events.

#### 19.1a.3 Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Addressing Climate Change Impacts

Local policy-driven strategies can play a crucial role in addressing the impacts of climate change on urban equity. These strategies can include policies that promote sustainable and resilient urban development, as well as initiatives that aim to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and mitigate the effects of climate change.

For example, local governments can implement policies that promote the use of renewable energy sources, such as solar or wind power, to reduce their carbon footprint and mitigate the effects of climate change. They can also implement policies that promote sustainable urban development, such as green building codes or incentives for green roofs, to increase the resilience of urban areas to climate change impacts.

In addition, local governments can also implement initiatives that aim to reduce the vulnerability of marginalized communities to climate change impacts. This can include providing resources for evacuation or rebuilding after extreme weather events, as well as implementing policies that promote equitable access to resources and services.

#### 19.1a.4 Conclusion

Climate change is a significant threat to urban areas, particularly for marginalized communities who are often disproportionately affected by its impacts. Local policy-driven strategies can play a crucial role in addressing these issues, promoting sustainable and resilient urban development, and reducing the vulnerability of marginalized communities to climate change impacts. As the effects of climate change continue to intensify, it is essential for local governments to implement these strategies to create more equitable and sustainable urban areas.




### Subsection: 19.1b The Role of Climate Change in Urban Equity

Climate change plays a significant role in urban equity, exacerbating existing inequalities and creating new challenges for marginalized communities. As urban areas continue to grow and face the impacts of climate change, it is crucial to understand the role of climate change in urban equity and develop strategies to address these issues.

#### 19.1b.1 Climate Change and Marginalized Communities

Marginalized communities, particularly those living in urban areas, are disproportionately affected by the impacts of climate change. These communities often live in areas that are more vulnerable to the effects of climate change, such as low-lying coastal areas or informal settlements. They also lack the resources and infrastructure to mitigate these impacts, making them more susceptible to the consequences of climate change.

Climate change can exacerbate existing inequalities in urban areas. For example, marginalized communities may face increased health risks from extreme weather events, such as heatwaves and floods. These events can also lead to loss of housing, employment, and other essential services, further exacerbating their vulnerability.

#### 19.1b.2 Climate Change and Urban Policy

Local policy-driven strategies can play a crucial role in addressing the impacts of climate change on urban equity. These strategies can include policies that promote sustainable and resilient urban development, as well as initiatives that aim to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and mitigate the effects of climate change.

One example of a local policy-driven strategy is the implementation of urban climatology in decision-making for municipal planning and policy. Urban climatology can help identify areas at risk of extreme heat events, floods, and other climate-related hazards. This information can inform the development of policies and initiatives that aim to reduce these risks and protect marginalized communities.

Another strategy is the integration of climate change considerations into urban planning and development. This can include incorporating climate change projections into long-term planning, as well as implementing adaptive and resilience-building strategies. For example, incorporating green infrastructure, such as green roofs and permeable pavement, can help mitigate the impacts of climate change, such as heatwaves and flooding.

#### 19.1b.3 The Role of Urban Resilience

Urban resilience is a crucial aspect of addressing the impacts of climate change on urban equity. Resilience-boosting strategies can help communities prepare for and recover from the impacts of climate change. These strategies can include community-based adaptation, which involves engaging marginalized communities in the planning and implementation of adaptation measures.

In addition to building resilience, it is also essential to address the root causes of urban inequalities. This can include policies that promote social and economic equity, as well as initiatives that aim to reduce poverty and improve access to essential services. By addressing these underlying issues, we can create more equitable and sustainable urban areas that are better equipped to face the challenges of climate change.





### Section: 19.1c Strategies for Climate Resilient and Equitable Cities

As we have seen in the previous section, climate change has a significant impact on urban equity. It exacerbates existing inequalities and creates new challenges for marginalized communities. However, with the right strategies, we can build climate-resilient and equitable cities that can withstand the impacts of climate change.

#### 19.1c.1 Urban Climatology and Spatial Planning

Urban climatology plays a crucial role in decision-making for municipal planning and policy. By understanding the impacts of climate change on urban areas, we can develop strategies to mitigate these impacts and protect marginalized communities. For example, by using urban climatology to identify areas at risk of extreme heat events, we can implement policies and initiatives to reduce these risks.

Spatial planning is also essential in addressing the impacts of climate change on urban equity. By considering the spatial distribution of different urban areas, we can identify areas that are more vulnerable to climate change and develop targeted strategies to address their specific needs. This can include policies that promote sustainable and resilient development in these areas, as well as initiatives that aim to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and mitigate the effects of climate change.

#### 19.1c.2 Resilience-Boosting Strategies

In addition to spatial planning, there are other strategies that can help build resilience in urban areas. These include promoting green infrastructure, such as green roofs and rain gardens, which can help mitigate the impacts of extreme weather events. We can also implement policies that encourage the use of renewable energy sources, reducing our reliance on fossil fuels and reducing our carbon footprint.

Furthermore, we can develop community-based adaptation strategies, which involve working closely with marginalized communities to identify and address their specific needs and vulnerabilities. This can include providing resources and support for these communities to adapt to the impacts of climate change.

#### 19.1c.3 The Role of Public Health

Public health is also a crucial aspect of building resilience in urban areas. As we have seen, extreme heat events, floods, and other climate-related hazards can have significant impacts on the health of urban dwellers. Therefore, it is essential to consider the health implications of climate change when developing strategies for resilience.

This can include implementing policies that promote healthy and sustainable living, such as promoting active transportation and providing access to fresh and nutritious food options. We can also develop public health initiatives that aim to educate and prepare urban dwellers for the impacts of climate change, such as heat wave preparedness plans and flood evacuation protocols.

#### 19.1c.4 The Importance of Equity

Finally, it is crucial to consider equity when developing strategies for climate resilience. Marginalized communities are often the most vulnerable to the impacts of climate change, and it is essential to ensure that these communities are not left behind in our efforts to build resilience.

This can include implementing policies that promote social and economic equity, such as affordable housing initiatives and job training programs. We can also develop targeted strategies for marginalized communities, such as providing resources and support for these communities to adapt to the impacts of climate change.

In conclusion, building climate-resilient and equitable cities requires a multifaceted approach that considers the spatial distribution of urban areas, promotes resilience-boosting strategies, and prioritizes public health and equity. By working together, we can create cities that are prepared and equipped to face the challenges of climate change.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of climate change and urban equity. We have seen how the impacts of climate change disproportionately affect marginalized communities, particularly those living in urban areas. We have also discussed the role of local policies in addressing these issues and promoting equity in the face of climate change.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of considering the social and economic implications of climate change when developing policies. As we have seen, climate change can exacerbate existing inequalities and create new challenges for marginalized communities. Therefore, it is crucial for policymakers to prioritize equity in their climate change strategies.

Another important aspect to consider is the role of community involvement in addressing climate change. By involving marginalized communities in the decision-making process, we can ensure that their needs and concerns are addressed in policies and programs. This can also help build trust and promote a sense of ownership among these communities, leading to more effective and sustainable solutions.

Overall, it is clear that climate change and urban equity are complex and interconnected issues that require a multifaceted approach. By incorporating equity considerations into local policies and involving marginalized communities in the process, we can work towards creating more just and resilient cities in the face of climate change.

Consider factors such as access to resources, vulnerability to extreme weather events, and economic implications. Use this information to develop recommendations for local policies that prioritize equity in addressing climate change.

## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City

### Introduction:

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of equity and inclusion has become a crucial aspect of urban planning and development. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is essential to ensure that all members of the community have equal access to resources and opportunities. This is especially true in the context of economic development, where the distribution of wealth and opportunities can greatly impact the well-being of a city and its residents.

In this chapter, we will explore the relationship between equity and inclusion in the context of economic development. We will discuss the various factors that contribute to economic inequality and how it affects different communities within a city. We will also examine the role of local policies and strategies in promoting equity and inclusion, and how they can be used to create a more just and equitable city.

Through this chapter, we hope to provide a comprehensive understanding of the complex and ever-evolving topic of equity and inclusion in economic development. By the end, readers will have a better understanding of the challenges and opportunities that arise in creating a more equitable and inclusive city, and the role that local policies and strategies play in achieving this goal. 





#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of climate change and urban equity, and how these two critical issues are intertwined. We have seen how climate change disproportionately affects marginalized communities, particularly those in urban areas, and how this can exacerbate existing social and economic inequalities. We have also discussed the importance of incorporating equity and inclusion considerations into climate change policies and strategies, to ensure that all communities have equal access to resources and opportunities to adapt and mitigate the impacts of climate change.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to addressing climate change and urban equity. This involves not only addressing the environmental aspects of climate change, but also considering the social and economic implications. It requires a deep understanding of the complex interactions between these factors, and a commitment to addressing them in a way that promotes equity and inclusion.

Another important point to note is the role of local policies and strategies in addressing climate change and urban equity. As we have seen, national and international policies and agreements are crucial, but they are not enough. Local policies and strategies are often the first line of defense for communities facing the impacts of climate change, and they can be tailored to the specific needs and characteristics of each community. This is particularly important in promoting equity and inclusion, as local policies can be designed to address the unique challenges faced by marginalized communities.

In conclusion, climate change and urban equity are two critical issues that cannot be addressed in isolation. They are deeply intertwined, and require a holistic and localized approach to address them effectively. By incorporating equity and inclusion considerations into climate change policies and strategies, we can work towards creating a more just and sustainable future for all.

### Introduction:

As we delve into the future of urban equity planning, it is important to note that the future is not a fixed entity, but rather a dynamic and ever-changing landscape. The future of urban equity planning is shaped by a multitude of factors, including technological advancements, societal shifts, and policy decisions. In this chapter, we will explore these factors and their potential impact on the future of urban equity planning.

One of the key factors that will shape the future of urban equity planning is technology. With the rapid advancement of technology, cities are becoming more interconnected and data-driven. This presents both opportunities and challenges for urban equity planning. On one hand, technology can provide valuable data and insights that can inform policy decisions and promote equity. On the other hand, it can also exacerbate existing inequalities if not used ethically and equitably.

Societal shifts, such as changes in demographics and cultural values, will also play a significant role in shaping the future of urban equity planning. As cities become more diverse and globalized, it is crucial for urban equity planning to adapt and address the needs and concerns of different communities. This includes addressing issues of representation and inclusion in decision-making processes.

Policy decisions, both at the local and national level, will also have a profound impact on the future of urban equity planning. Policies such as affordable housing initiatives, minimum wage increases, and job training programs can help promote equity and reduce inequalities. However, policies can also perpetuate or exacerbate inequalities if they are not carefully designed and implemented.

In this chapter, we will explore these factors in more detail and discuss potential strategies for addressing them in the context of urban equity planning. By understanding the future of urban equity planning, we can better prepare for and navigate the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead. 


# Title: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City":

## Chapter: - Chapter 20: Future of Urban Equity Planning:




### Subsection: 20.1a Emerging Trends in Urban Equity Planning

As we look towards the future of urban equity planning, it is important to consider the emerging trends that will shape the landscape of cities. These trends include the rise of smart cities, the increasing importance of public health in urban planning, and the incorporation of new planning theories and policies.

#### The Rise of Smart Cities

The concept of smart cities, where technology is used to improve the efficiency and sustainability of urban areas, is gaining traction in urban equity planning. With the increasing availability of data and advancements in technology, cities are able to collect and analyze data to inform policy decisions and promote equity. For example, data on traffic patterns can inform the placement of public transportation and bike lanes, reducing barriers to access for marginalized communities. Additionally, data on air quality can inform policies to reduce pollution and improve public health.

#### Public Health and Urban Planning

The impact of urban climatology on public health is becoming a growing concern in urban equity planning. As cities continue to expand and urbanization increases, the negative effects of pollution, extreme heat events, and stormwater on public health are becoming more apparent. Urban planners are now incorporating public health considerations into their decision-making processes, prioritizing policies that promote healthy and livable communities for all residents.

#### New Planning Theories and Policies

As urban areas continue to grow and face new challenges, urban planners are adopting new theories and policies to address these issues. For example, the concept of Blue Zones, which prioritize healthy living and longevity, is being incorporated into urban planning to create areas within the city that promote healthy lifestyles and improve the quality of life for residents. Additionally, policies such as congestion charges and prioritizing public transit and cycling are being implemented to reduce traffic congestion and promote sustainable transportation options.

#### Theories of Planning Procedure

Theories of planning procedure, such as the rational-comprehensive approach, the incremental approach, and the transactive approach, remain the principal theories of planning procedure today. However, new theories are also emerging, such as the communicative approach, the advocacy approach, and the equity approach. These theories emphasize the importance of community involvement and participation in the planning process, as well as addressing issues of equity and inclusion in decision-making.

#### Conclusion

As we look towards the future of urban equity planning, it is important to consider these emerging trends and their potential impact on the landscape of cities. By incorporating technology, prioritizing public health, and adopting new planning theories and policies, we can work towards creating more equitable and inclusive cities for all residents. 





### Subsection: 20.1b Challenges and Opportunities for Urban Equity Planning

As we look towards the future of urban equity planning, it is important to consider the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead. These challenges and opportunities will shape the direction of urban equity planning and will require innovative and collaborative solutions.

#### Challenges for Urban Equity Planning

One of the main challenges for urban equity planning is the unequal distribution of resources and opportunities within cities. As cities continue to grow and gentrify, marginalized communities are often displaced and face barriers to accessing basic needs such as housing, education, and healthcare. This creates a complex and interconnected set of challenges that must be addressed in order to promote equity and inclusion in urban areas.

Another challenge is the lack of data and resources for marginalized communities. Many marginalized communities, particularly those that are low-income or minority, face barriers to accessing technology and data that could inform policy decisions. This creates a power imbalance and further exacerbates existing inequalities.

#### Opportunities for Urban Equity Planning

Despite these challenges, there are also opportunities for urban equity planning. The rise of smart cities presents an opportunity to use technology and data to promote equity and inclusion. By incorporating data and technology into policy decisions, urban planners can identify and address disparities in access to resources and opportunities.

Additionally, the increasing focus on public health in urban planning presents an opportunity to prioritize the well-being of all residents. By considering the impact of urban climatology on public health, urban planners can implement policies that promote healthy and livable communities for all residents.

#### Collaborative Solutions

Addressing the challenges and opportunities for urban equity planning will require collaborative solutions. Urban planners must work closely with community members, particularly those from marginalized communities, to identify and address their needs and concerns. This can be achieved through community-based participatory research and policy-making, where community members are involved in the decision-making process.

Furthermore, partnerships between different sectors, such as government, academia, and non-profit organizations, can also help address the challenges and opportunities for urban equity planning. By working together, these sectors can bring diverse perspectives and resources to the table, leading to more comprehensive and effective solutions.

In conclusion, the future of urban equity planning presents both challenges and opportunities. By addressing these challenges and leveraging opportunities, urban planners can work towards creating more equitable and inclusive cities for all residents. Collaborative solutions and partnerships will be crucial in achieving this goal.





### Subsection: 20.1c Case Studies in Innovative Urban Equity Planning

As we look towards the future of urban equity planning, it is important to examine case studies of innovative urban equity planning strategies. These case studies can provide valuable insights and lessons learned for future urban equity planning efforts.

#### Case Study 1: The City of Portland, Oregon

The City of Portland, Oregon has been a leader in innovative urban equity planning. In 1996, the city implemented a comprehensive plan that prioritized equity and inclusion in all aspects of urban development. This plan included policies to address issues of affordable housing, transportation, and economic development. The city also established a Office of Equity and Human Rights to ensure that equity and inclusion were integrated into all city policies and programs.

One of the key strategies used by Portland was the use of community-based participatory research (CBPR). CBPR involves collaboration between researchers, community members, and other stakeholders to address community issues. In Portland, CBPR was used to identify and address disparities in access to resources and opportunities for marginalized communities. This approach has been successful in promoting equity and inclusion in the city.

#### Case Study 2: The City of Boston, Massachusetts

The City of Boston, Massachusetts has also been a leader in innovative urban equity planning. In 2015, the city released a plan called "Boston Creates" which aimed to promote equity and inclusion in all aspects of urban development. This plan included policies to address issues of affordable housing, education, and economic development. The city also established a Office of Equity and Inclusion to ensure that equity and inclusion were integrated into all city policies and programs.

One of the key strategies used by Boston was the use of data and technology to promote equity and inclusion. The city implemented a data-driven approach to identify and address disparities in access to resources and opportunities for marginalized communities. This approach has been successful in promoting equity and inclusion in the city.

#### Lessons Learned

These case studies demonstrate the importance of incorporating innovative strategies, such as community-based participatory research and data-driven approaches, in urban equity planning. They also highlight the importance of establishing policies and programs that prioritize equity and inclusion in all aspects of urban development. By learning from these successful examples, we can continue to improve and innovate urban equity planning for the future.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the future of urban equity planning and its potential impact on the just city. We have discussed the importance of incorporating equity and inclusion into local policy-driven strategies for economic development, and how these strategies can create a more equitable and inclusive urban environment for all residents. We have also examined the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead in the implementation of these strategies, and the role that community engagement and collaboration will play in their success.

As we move towards a more diverse and globalized society, it is crucial that we continue to prioritize equity and inclusion in our urban planning efforts. By addressing the needs and concerns of marginalized communities, we can create a more just and sustainable city for all. This will require a shift in mindset and a commitment to collaboration and inclusivity in all aspects of urban development.

In conclusion, the future of urban equity planning is bright, but it will require a collective effort from all stakeholders to achieve true equity and inclusion in our cities. By incorporating equity and inclusion into our local policies and strategies, we can create a more just and equitable urban environment for all residents.

#### Exercise 3: Policy Analysis

#### Exercise 4: Collaborative Planning

#### Exercise 5: Reflecting on Equity and Inclusion
Reflect on your own beliefs and attitudes towards equity and inclusion. How have these beliefs and attitudes been shaped by your experiences and surroundings? How can you incorporate equity and inclusion into your own actions and decisions?

By addressing the needs and concerns of marginalized communities, we can create a more just and sustainable city for all. ## Chapter: Equity & Inclusion: Local Policy-Driven Strategies for Economic Development & the Just City

### Introduction:

In today's rapidly changing world, the concept of a just city is becoming increasingly important. As urban populations continue to grow and resources become scarcer, it is crucial for cities to address issues of equity and inclusion in order to create a sustainable and livable future for all residents. This is especially true in the context of economic development, where the distribution of resources and opportunities can have a significant impact on the well-being of different communities.

In this chapter, we will explore the role of local policy in promoting equity and inclusion in economic development. We will examine how policies can be used to address issues of access to resources, opportunities, and services, and how they can be tailored to meet the specific needs and challenges of different communities. We will also discuss the importance of community engagement and participation in the policy-making process, and how it can lead to more effective and sustainable solutions.

Through a combination of case studies, research, and analysis, we will delve into the various strategies and approaches that have been implemented in different cities around the world. From affordable housing initiatives to job training programs, we will examine the successes and challenges of these policies and their impact on the overall equity and inclusion of urban communities.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complex and multifaceted nature of equity and inclusion in economic development, and the crucial role that local policy plays in creating a just city for all.
